Amateur Ramblings

New Developments and Trends in Japan's Invasion of China 213

— Shao Xiang

Since the "Tanggu Truce," people have believed that Japan's predatory behavior towards us has come to an end. Little did they know that although the sound of imperialist Japan's cannons attacking North China has ceased on the surface, in reality, not only have the Japanese troops in the war zone not withdrawn, and the various ports along the Chang River have not been returned, but also North China, Mongolia, and even South China and Fujian have been subjected to new threats from Japan's economic, political, and military forces. Judging from the current situation, not only will the quantity of Japanese goods dumped increase day by day, not only will the activities of Chinese traitors bought by the Japanese side become more rampant, but also the Japanese army has the possibility of attacking China again and plundering Chinese territory.

We know that after the "September 18th" Incident, because the people of the country worked hard to boycott Japanese goods, for a time, Japanese trade with China almost completely stopped, and it suffered a very serious blow economically. However, not long after, our boycott movement declined due to various reasons, and Japanese trade with China not only gradually restored its original state, but also had new developments. According to business circles, "According to the recent announcement by the Japanese Commercial Office, in the first half of this year, Japanese trade with China has indeed shown an improving trend. The total value of imports and exports is JPY 111,125,200, an increase of JPY 25,591,000 compared to the same period last year. The export of Japanese goods to China totaled JPY 51,154,200, an increase of JPY 2,762,000 compared to the same period last year. If the Northeast and Hong Kong are added, the total trade volume reaches JPY 300 million, occupying an absolutely superior position in the trade of various countries with China. After the implementation of the new tariff, it has provided convenience for the import of Japanese goods, and the export to China in the second half of this year should have a significant increase. The movement to boycott Japanese goods in the north and south has almost completely disappeared in the first half of this year and is no longer a problem." (A report from a certain newspaper on the 29th) 丨丨 This is a new record and prediction of Japan's economic aggression against China.

At the same time, in order to establish its so-called "South China Policy," the Governor-General of Taiwan specially convened the "Five-Prefecture Conference on the Other Shore" recently. In this meeting, in addition to some of the most important proposals related to Japan's invasion of China, which are impossible to know because the Japanese side strictly maintains secrecy, there are also these noteworthy resolutions 丨

One, promote the doctrine of "Sino-Japanese Friendship" as the guiding principle;

One, dump coal in South China;

One, open up the Taiwan pineapple canned food market in China;

One, guide and reward the colonial industry of registered residents.

What does this mean? Our answer is: Japanese imperialism not only wants to annex North China, but also covets South China, and attempts to enslave the entire Chinese nation under the guise of "promoting the doctrine of 'Sino-Japanese Friendship'" 丨

As for North China and Mongolia, they are even more regarded by Japanese imperialism as "spheres of influence," and everything can be freely handled by them, and outsiders are not allowed to interfere. Recently, the Japanese side stated that all military exercises by the powers in North China must be notified to Japan in advance, which is an example of it already considering North China as its own. As for its military and political activities in Mongolia, openly buying Chinese traitors in North China, freely recruiting troops, and establishing political groups, they are even more blatant manifestations of its ambition to annex North China. Recently, various parties have widely spread the rumor that Japan will send troops to invade Suiyuan and Chahar within a few months: although this may not be credible, everyone knows that the fierce and sinister Japanese imperialism is eager to annex North China. The question is when and under what circumstances it will begin to act. If the time is right, the Japanese army can start attacking us under any pretext. Wasn't the Zangben Incident not long ago an ugly drama in which Japan wanted to coerce us with the pretext of the disappearance of its diplomats in China? From this, it can be seen that as long as the time is right, Japanese imperialism can do anything. However, judging from the current situation, the possibility of Japan opening fire on China again is indeed likely to happen at any time!

However, China is not simply the market of Japan alone, but a semi-colony jointly ruled by international imperialism, especially Britain, Japan, and the United States. The result of Japan's continuous attacks on China will inevitably directly harm the interests of the powers, especially Britain and the United States, so as to cause serious conflicts between them, and even lead to war. The warlords and politicians in Tokyo have also seen this, but in order to save the economic and political crisis in their country, and in order to gain a superior position in future wars, they have to take advantage of the current conflict situation of the European and American powers, and desperately launch various attacks on China, so as to quickly ignite the fire on the Pacific. Therefore, in the final analysis, the only destination of Japan's desperate invasion of China is to go to war, a cruel war 丨

Under this circumstance, China naturally has the possibility of becoming a victim of Japan and British, American and other imperialists, which is very dangerous: but at the same time, it is also an excellent opportunity for us to use the conflicts of imperialist powers, when all their own crises converge, to seek independence and find a way out. Therefore, we do not need to fear the attacks of Japan and all imperialists, but should take the opportunity to rise up and seek our own liberation. What is terrible is that we close our eyes and do not see the current situation, and always sleep without moving, allowing the enemy to slaughter and destroy us 丨

Life

Clerk 214

— Dasheng

Under the current social system, a group of graduates from primary and secondary schools, outstanding students of old-fashioned teachers, and people who have received a little education under certain circumstances, because of their weak knowledge and abilities, are mostly difficult to obtain important positions in the current society. Their "superficial understanding" or even "ununderstanding" of academic ability determines their tragic future. They cannot avoid becoming victims of the times; they are difficult to have excellent gains in the vocational world, and even if they do, it is difficult to be competent for happy service. They did not load much "stuff" into their bellies earlier, and in this day of intensified and profound survival competition, it is natural that few of them will not fail miserably. (People with stuff in their bellies are now in the same fate.)

But they can still write well. Most of them also have the ability to endure hardship and work hard. Relying on this ability, they may not be able to exchange it for bread. The position of a clerk is not completely lacking or completely unfindable.

In this short article, I would like to describe a little about the lives of this type of people who take copying as their main job, and who may be called "clerks" or "assistants" in name

Page 20

or "private secretaries." First of all, I want to talk about the hardship of the work of these people and the disproportion between the reward paid for this hardship. First, let's observe the hardship of the lives of the clerks in schools at all levels. Their more important work is mostly copying and mimeographing handouts, announcements, notices, official documents, letters, and other documents in the school. In universities, clerks have a more precise division of labor in their duties. The clerk in the president's office does not take care of the affairs of the dean's office or the registrar's office, and those who write mimeographs are only confined to their own small room and are accompanied by wax paper and steel plates. The situation in middle schools is relatively different. A clerk often serves as a staff member of the academic affairs office, and also takes care of the written matters of moral education and administrative affairs. Sometimes, he has to accept the trust and instructions from the president's office in his busy schedule. The clerk in the primary school is even more omnipotent. Almost all the copying and mimeographing matters in the entire school can hardly do without his wonderful hand.

Among the above three types of clerks, there is no doubt that the one who serves in the primary school is the most 　　 and gets the lowest reward. In the public primary schools in the counties of Jiangsu and Zhejiang where education is relatively developed, it must be considered a good thing if a clerk can exchange fifteen yuan a month for eight hours of blood and sweat. Last year, the author visited two large-scale county-run complete primary schools with as many as six or seven hundred students in Pudong and Nanhui. Each school hired a clerk with a monthly salary of fifteen yuan. Under the situation of exhausted educational funds in other provinces, few primary school clerks can get this amount. The situation in this city is similar. The author also paid this amount of monthly salary to the clerk of a primary school attached to a middle school that he used to work in in this city. What is said above is a more scaled higher and lower elementary school. Those primary schools with few students and simple facilities naturally cannot afford this amount at all, and most of them cannot afford such an employee at all. As for junior primary schools, in the case where the principal兼任the servant, it is almost a myth to say that they can hire a clerk. As for the majority of private primary schools, for the sake of poor income, their abacus will never be set to such a wasteful additional expenditure.

Middle school clerks can usually earn a monthly salary of twenty yuan in more scaled schools. Assuming that you "have served in the school for many years and have made outstanding achievements," your monthly salary can easily be increased to twenty-five yuan or thirty yuan due to the development of the school. If you want to rise further, then your hope may become a fantasy that is not easy to realize.

Now let's talk about the treatment of clerks in universities. A clerk (often兼任secretary) serving in the president's office can receive a monthly salary of forty to sixty yuan. Although the situation in each school is not exactly the same, the difference is limited. The highest monthly income of clerks who write mimeographing handouts is difficult to exceed thirty yuan, and most of them are around twenty-five yuan. Those who serve in the president's office are mostly confidants of the school authorities or students of this school, while those who write mimeographs are mostly hired for their expertise in copying techniques. Due to the different qualifications, abilities, and positions, the rewards naturally cannot be equal.

Now I would like to talk about their suffering. Copying is originally an extremely mechanical and boring job, and anyone is afraid that they will not welcome it very much. But the most mechanical and unbearable of all copying work is probably mimeographing. No matter how expert a person is in this area, few of them will not frown at the wax paper, steel plate, and steel pen. They may write very well, but the words that appear on the wax paper are not beautiful enough; some problems caused by the poor quality of the wax paper and the steel pen and steel plate itself will further increase their impatience and annoyance. If you randomly grab one of these mimeographing experts and ask, you will immediately find that he talks about it with no shaking his head and sighing. Especially during the big and small exams, it is even more of an emergency when they are about to lose their lives. Mr. Ting's exam questions are also sent to be printed, and that Mr.'s exam questions are also sent to be printed. The teachers are all busy people, and they do not prepare early. They often send the exam questions the day before the exam. The exam questions of all the teachers are concentrated together, and the time is so urgent. In the midst of a thousand busyness, few of them do not make special sacrifices, "burning the midnight oil" all night, in order to avoid mistakes and falls in their duties, and get through this difficult time. Every semester, there are always a few days of tense days when they cannot sleep well. Some schools, especially primary schools, not only have to "write" themselves, but also have to "print" themselves. This hardship is of course even more advanced. Of course, schools are not the only ones that hire clerks. Various social, industrial, commercial, military, and political organizations also have some documents to be copied, and they all inevitably need this kind of talent. Their treatment in these various aspects cannot be exactly the same, but one thing is the same and deeply known to us, that is, their status is low, and everything must be subject to the command of superior staff. There is no freedom of will for themselves. They are only a puppet to be used. Their income is not difficult to infer from this position.

We don't have to worry about the misfortune of this group of people. After all, they are still people who have a legitimate occupation and can live on their own. There is a kind of people in the world who have higher qualifications and abilities and are also making a living by this copying job. I think they are a more unfortunate group of people. We know that there are countless unemployed college students, primary and secondary school teachers, and cultural people now. As long as they have a way to live on their own, no matter what kind of blood and sweat they have to pay, they may be happy to accept some difficult job. Scholars, celebrities, and experts often hire an "assistant" or "private secretary" and the like. The main purpose is to find someone to copy manuscripts, help collect materials, and cut, paste, sort, and organize various materials. This provides a way out for the group of people mentioned above. They naturally cannot get a salary based on their qualifications, and they will not get a high salary for their mechanical work. Scholars, celebrities, and experts do not necessarily hire "assistants" for a long time. After a certain job is completed, he will ask you to "rest" for a while, and he will come to "notify" you when a new job arrives. Their method of remuneration is not necessarily calculated on a monthly basis, but there are also those who use the "piecework system." If calculated on a monthly basis, they can generally pay thirty to forty yuan per month. If calculated on a piecework basis, each thousand words will not be less than two dimes of silver. In the past, a classmate who served in another area became unemployed midway and found his main professor. That gentleman gave his student some copying work and sent him thirty yuan a month. That classmate worked for two months and then went to find his own way. Another professor hired an assistant among the students and assigned him some copying manuscripts, clipping newspapers, and going to cultural institutions to copy relevant materials, and paid him forty yuan a month as remuneration. As for calculating by the word, the fastest in eight hours may not be able to copy 10,000 words, and even 7,000 or 8,000 words will take a lot of effort; as a result of burying your head at the desk all day, you only get more than one yuan. Also, this kind of clerk is often sent to various famous social organizations, such as big newspapers, big libraries, big factories, big banks... to copy some ready-made statistical and research materials. In winter, you cannot use the fact that your hands are frozen as a reason to say that you want to rest for a day or two; in this summer, you cannot make excuses because too much sweat is flowing, so as to delay the master's research. For the sake of life, you have to endure everything. It is understandable that you are a slave to your job; but if you ignore the reason for this, I think it is unforgivable.

Common Sense

Deer Industry 215

— Jieren

Everyone probably knows about deer! Don't you often read stories about deer in books? This is a beautiful and very docile animal, with a body covered with shiny brownish-yellow fine hair, interspersed with many white spots. The brownish-yellow body is scattered with circles of pure white small dots, which is really beautiful! Therefore, it is also called "spotted deer" or "sika deer". Deer also have a pair of slender, branching horns on their heads, like the top scholar who adds two flowers to his gauze hat in old operas. It is not wrong to compare it to the top scholar, as its beautiful coat is not like the top scholar's return home in glory at that time? Its place of origin is the interior of Taiwan that we have lost, where people set traps to catch it, but most of them are specially raised at home and transported to our China for sale. This kind of deer is also produced in our Guandong area, but the number is small. And the deer in Guandong is better than the deer in Taiwan, but the cost is higher and it cannot be used. So what are these deer used for? They are all used as medicinal materials. The "Whole Deer Pills" and "Deer Horn Glue" in Chinese medicine shops are made of deer. And "Deer Velvet" is the newly born horn of the deer, which is even more valuable.

In the early years, deer from Taiwan were all brought by sailboats and unloaded at the Zhenhai port in Zhejiang. They were sold to dealers in the area. New deer were transported every year in February and March, but most of them were still young and had to be raised for a few more months before they could be sold. The number transported each time was not very large, ranging from ten to twenty or thirty. In total, there were only more than one hundred in the whole year. Once they were transported and paid, the responsibility rested on the shoulders of the agent dealers. Of course, the bank had to open up another place specifically for them to be raised. A long row of wooden fences tied the deer one by one there. Green grass was the only food, which was hired to cut from the fields. They had to be fed four or five times a day. When feeding, two or three people had to give it separately, otherwise, if they saw grass on the other side, they would want to grab it, so the whole fence would be restless. In winter, the green grass was withered. At this time, wheat and sweet potato vines were mostly used instead. These deer also get sick. As long as you see them staying still and not eating anything, you should find a way to treat them; if they unfortunately die, you should immediately write a letter to notify the other party, and you must leave the entire skin and four feet of the deer as evidence, which is also to show your sincerity.

The way to sell deer is based on the weight. However, it also depends on how the sales are in the market and how many are transported. If the sales are good in the market and few are transported, they can naturally be sold at a good price; otherwise, few people will inquire about them. Therefore, it may cost one or two yuan per catty, or even less, it is hard to say. A deer can weigh as little as seventy or eighty catties on a balance scale, then it can always be sold for seventy or eighty yuan. Compared with the refugees in the disaster area who sell their children for a price of ten or twenty yuan and no one wants them, it can be said that people are not as good as beasts! Because each catty has a value, when both parties agree to deliver the goods, the buddies in those lines secretly and recklessly force the deer to eat the grass, and even mix stones in the grass in the wooden cage, hoping to increase the weight. In fact, how much weight can it add? It's really a despicable and ridiculous thing! Each buyer wants to buy a few, and there is no manipulation and monopoly. This point is commendable. At that time, the one with the largest sales volume was Hu Qingyutang in Hangzhou, which could sell dozens of them a year; followed by Ye Zhongdetang in Hangzhou. The rest could not match them, like a small wizard seeing a great wizard.

Each batch of deer was transported and sold, and the busy situation suddenly made the always quiet air lively. One by one the wooden cages containing deer were placed in the square, and many curious people gathered around, and some deliberately provoked them to joke. It is said that when deer are killed, they must also be sacrificed to the gods, hung up, and paraded around. The former is indeed a ridiculous superstitious act, while the latter is an advertisement to let everyone know that the products of a certain pharmacy do not deceive people with fake products.

In the past four or five years, because pirates have been rampant on the ocean, entire sailboats have often been kidnapped. If they are transported by steamship, the cost is too high, resulting in no profit. Moreover, due to the relationship of the boycott movement (Taiwan is no longer owned by our country. Naturally, it is the same example.) Therefore, deer from Taiwan are no longer transported and can be said to have disappeared. However, the main reason is that small-scale deer farms have been established in Lanxi and Cixi, Zhejiang, specifically for breeding. However, the sales of deer are not as good as before, which is also undeniable. Because deer is used as a tonic, you think, now there are many people who don't even have anything to eat, will they still think about tonics?

Small Monograph

China's Wheat Industry Amidst Global Recession 216

— Tie Bing

Wheat is not only the main food in northern China, but also an indispensable food in European and American countries. Therefore, when discussing life, Chinese people often talk about "rice bowls," while foreigners all say "bread." From this, it can be seen that wheat and flour are indeed a very noteworthy issue in the food problem.

People often mistakenly believe that only the north produces wheat because northerners eat noodles and southerners eat rice. Although the northern provinces are very rich in wheat production, there are also many places south of the Yangtze River that produce wheat. Jiangsu, Hubei, and Anhui provinces have an annual output of more than 30 million dan, which is not much less than Henan and Shandong, which are more important producing areas. Now, let's list the total wheat production of our country in the past three years as follows:

Republic of China Year 20 389 million dan

Republic of China Year 21 401

Republic of China Year 22 2290

This number seems quite impressive on the surface; but in reality, it is not. If we try to compare the number of foreign wheat exports in the past three years with the numbers listed above, we can see the seriousness of China's wheat production problem.

Republic of China Year 20 2.2 million dan

Republic of China Year 21 15

Republic of China Year 22 17

That is to say, although our country's wheat production is quite abundant, we still have to import 20 million dan (worth about 100 million yuan) of foreign wheat every year. This is such a painful fact!

Some domestic economic experts, because they see that our country imports 20 million dan of foreign wheat every year, superficially explain that "China's wheat production cannot be self-sufficient," which is completely nonsense. They only see the alarming amount of imports, but forget that this alarming amount is entirely because of the inconvenience of inland transportation, etc., so that the manufacturers in various commercial ports have to purchase foreign wheat.

At present, the farmers in China who grow wheat are facing the oppression of high-interest loans and exorbitant taxes on the one hand, and the blow of falling wheat prices on the other hand. Regarding the situation of high-interest loans and exorbitant taxes, let's put it aside for the time being. Now let's take a look at the actual situation of wheat prices.

Twenty years ago, the average value of domestic wheat was about five yuan per dan. Ten years ago, the average value was about six yuan, but recently, it is rare to see a market price that can exceed four yuan. In addition, with the gradual decline in the price of foreign wheat, domestic wheat has a tendency to become unrecoverable.

Although the price of domestic wheat is declining, because its quality is slightly worse, the flour industry still purchases foreign wheat. The result of purchasing foreign wheat in this way is that it has promoted a large amount of import surplus on the one hand, but has also hindered the sales of domestic wheat and lowered the price of domestic wheat on the other hand. Foreign wheat continues to pour in, and domestic wheat continues to decline. As a result, it has not only created a crisis for domestic wheat, but has also created a crisis for the domestic flour industry. We can understand this by just looking at the recent sharp decline in the sales of domestic flour and the sharp drop in its price.

The flour sold in Shanghai from January to March this year only accounted for 70% of the same period last year. The flour price also only accounted for 85% of the same period last year. The output even fell to 46% of the same period last year. If this continues, not only will the farmers have no place to sell and no way to live: even the manufacturers who run flour mills may find it difficult to live!

In order to save this terrible disaster, we believe that not only should the import tax on foreign wheat be increased, but also the improvement of the quality of domestic wheat, the abolition of exorbitant taxes, the prohibition of high-interest loans, the development of inland transportation, the encouragement of planting wheat fields, and the encouragement of using domestic wheat 　etc., must be given the greatest effort.

Amateur Work

Research on Wireless Radio 217

— Qing

Researching wireless radio is one of my amateur pursuits. In recent years, most of my spare time has been dedicated to it. Although this work only started in the twenty-first year of the Republic [1932], I am confident that I have gained considerable knowledge of wireless radio in these short two or three years. During my research, failure and success have alternated. I failed in my first attempt, and failed again in the second, but I was able to approach it with an indomitable spirit, and ultimately success belonged to me. The more I failed, the more I tried to research; the more I researched, the more I enjoyed it. For several years, I have been immersed in it day and night, and my joy has been boundless. Therefore, I hope that others will also engage in this pursuit. I now offer my humble opinions on the benefits of researching wireless radio and its preliminary methods, hoping that they will be welcomed by those who aspire to conduct self-study?

Wireless radio is one of the emerging industries. It is still considered quite developed in our country. Although we cannot keep pace with Europe and the United States, we can still follow closely behind. Especially in recent years, there has been significant progress. Society has a very urgent need for wireless radio specialists. All kinds of ship radio stations, aviation radio stations, meteorological radio stations, military radio stations, commercial radio stations, broadcasting stations, and other related fields of wireless radio manufacturing, repair, and management have a great need for such talent. Therefore, those with wireless radio skills can easily find a foothold in today's society where there is more grain than monks. If someone has the ambition to run a business, they can also take advantage of the opportunity when this new industry has not yet fully developed in China to establish a new business. This would help the country promote the development of this new industry and allow individuals to make a living. It is truly a win-win situation. Even if one does not want to make wireless radio a fixed profession, but only uses a part of one's spare time to research it as a hobby, the mental effort and time spent are still worthwhile. When I used my own strength to assemble my first radio and heard music in the earphones, my joy was truly beyond that of a king ruling from the south. Moreover, countless experiences and knowledge can be gained from this.

To those who are unfamiliar with wireless radio, wireless radio machines are often considered a mysterious and unfathomable work of ingenuity. In reality, even those who are unlearned can research and enjoy it. I once saw a technician in a wireless radio shop who was initially just an apprentice in that shop, unaware of what wireless radio was, but now he is actually teaching others how to make it eloquently. When starting research, one should read more books and magazines, and at the same time purchase some components and prepare appropriate tools, then one can begin to experiment. Initially, one should make the simplest crystal radio, then a single vacuum tube radio, and then gradually increase the number of vacuum tubes; from using dry batteries to using household electricity; from longwave to shortwave; from radio receivers to transmitters. In short, one should progress from simple to complex, from easy to difficult, so that knowledge and experience will naturally advance step by step. One must not be ambitious and aim too high, lest one is at a loss when difficulties arise. As for the most accessible and practical wireless radio books, to my knowledge, there are the six volumes of "Introduction to Wireless Radio" published by the Chung Hwa Book Company, the "Wireless Radio Reader" published by Shen Bao, and the six volumes of "Science Series" sold by the Asia-America Company at No. 323 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. All are simple and practical. Even those who do not know what wireless radio is can follow them to manufacture it themselves after reading. After increasing experience and knowledge, one can then gradually seek further advanced study. There is no other way to advance study than to experiment more and read more books.

Wireless radio is one of China's emerging industries. Its progress and hope are truly endless, and it is very worthwhile for us to engage in. I hope that those who aspire to this field will catch up quickly and not be discouraged by "lacking this knowledge," then the writing of this article will not be in vain.

Outlying Postal Agency

Drawing Water 218

— Manong

Changzhou Correspondence

This year, during the yellow plum season, there was no "plum rain," so farmers could only draw water to transplant rice seedlings. It takes five or six people to draw enough water to fill two or three mu of fields. As soon as the seedlings are transplanted, the water dries up. "Yellow seedlings" cannot withstand dryness, so they have to draw water again. The sun is scorching, and the dry soil around the fields absorbs too much water. Even if you add water, it won't last three days. The water dries up again, and the seedlings haven't taken root, so you have to add more. The river is shallow and the banks are steep, making it difficult to scoop water. It takes eighteen people to draw water for a whole day, and it's not enough to add a layer of water to two mu of rice fields. Therefore, this year, in the rice fields of Jiangnan, less than half can be transplanted. Three or four times more manpower than in previous years has been spent on drawing water to add water. Later, rivers, ponds, ditches, and dams successively dried up, leaving no water to draw. Even those that didn't dry up had to stop because it was too difficult to draw water. They put their energy, hope, and limited money into organizing a meeting to pray for rain. As the drought deepened, some blamed people for not being sincere, and others complained that the Bodhisattva was not effective. Millions of farmers held the same thoughts, facing the scorched earth of the "white fields" and the dry seedlings, which were scattered like the hair of a modern girl, with disappointment, anxiety, and worry. There were no sounds of waterwheels, no shouts of urging oxen. The entire countryside lay under an atmosphere of famine and death.

Recently, it has rained for a few days, but not much. The people hold onto the belief that "if it rains a little, it will rain more," and while the seedlings are still alive, they seize the opportunity to draw as much water as possible. They treat it like a mosquito net, sparing no expense to transport water from afar to the fields. So the waterwheels are working again.

Water wheels can be divided into several types according to their method of application. The ones that are cranked by hand are called small waterwheels. One type is cranked with both hands like punching, called a "punching waterwheel." The ones with a wider body that require two people to crank together up and down are called "dragon waterwheels." Large waterwheels are foot-operated, named according to the number of people needed to step on them, such as three-person waterwheels, Diamond waterwheels, six-person waterwheels, and nine-old-men waterwheels. The so-called Diamond waterwheel is a four-person waterwheel. The villagers avoid the number "four" because it sounds the same as "death," so they use the name Four Great Diamonds to replace it. The nine-person Nine Old Men waterwheel is the king of waterwheels. It is rarely used under normal circumstances unless it is a high water bank in such a severe drought as this year. In addition, there are ox-powered waterwheels, which are fixed waterwheels with mushroom-like thatched sheds covering the waterwheel banks. As for machine-powered waterwheels, because they are too expensive and have too many conditions, they are not yet very common in application.

Small waterwheels are almost completely ineffective this year. Along the long riverbanks, in the open spaces under the willow shade, you can see large waterwheels with six or nine people stepping on them, arranged like "connecting camps." In the struggle of sweating and swollen feet, the cries and the sound of the waterwheels miserably become a swan song, scaring the cicadas on the willow branches, making them dare not and unable to sing their high-pitched "I know, I know" song. Truly, the work on the axle is too difficult and arduous.

As soon as the east turns white, under the weary starlight, the water-drawing team starts work. The work allocation for a six-person waterwheel is: the two strongest men carry the heavy axle. The ones with sharp eyes and careful minds

Continued on page 5

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

Two people carry the long trough. In addition to the full trough of "Lianbi" [water-scooping leaves], they also have to carry hoes, iron shovels, and teapots, etc. The remaining two people are responsible for transporting stools, props, water ladders, straw curtains, and other equipment. A waterwheel is a rather complex machine, but the installation by a trained water-drawing team is quite scientific. Each person is transported to the destination, and everyone quickly divides the work and installs it. The two people who shovel the axle install the axle, pad the stools, drive in the props, and use the ropes and handrails [a straight, long fir wood] to carry the long trough, tie them to the props for everyone to lie on and step on the waterwheel. The people carrying the trough put the trough in place and connect the "dragon head Lianbi" to the gears of the axle, and put the water ladder into the water. The remaining two people use hoes to shovel and open the "dragon gate" [build a缺口], add lubricating oil to the rotating parts of the stools and axle, and spread the straw curtain on the props to provide shade. After the installation is complete, get on the waterwheel. The two people carrying the axle step on both ends of the axle, relying on the two sets of "footrests" of the props, called the left and right "front steps." The people carrying the scales occupy the left and right of the water gate where the dial teeth in the center of the axle and the Lianbi plate at the head of the trough are connected, called "holding the dragon gate." The remaining two people step on the empty space in the middle of the front step and the dragon gate, called the left and right "twisting silk steps." Twelve feet step together, of course, no one is allowed to be lazy and step in the air, but the two people stepping on the twisting silk steps are much easier. In addition to stepping with their feet, the people in the front steps must also pay attention to whether the props driven into the soil are strong and whether the rope knots tied to the handrails and straw curtains will break or loosen. The two people holding the dragon gate must pay attention to the depth of the water in the trough and whether the Lianbi leaves have problems with slipping or breaking. Because of the accumulated weight of six people, the water shock, and the wind attack, the waterwheel often has problems. The collapse of the prop is called "Taoluoshi," the rope break and the lever drop are called "Great New Year," and the Lianbi break is called "Returning the Dragon," which is often a dangerous accident that can kill people and damage the waterwheel. If such a danger occurs, then not only will they not get paid, but the boss will also hold the people in the front steps or dragon gate accountable based on the cause of the accident.

In such hot weather, it goes without saying how hot the water-drawing workers are who are working with their mouths, eyes, hands, and feet. The only way to avoid the heat is to draw water early. The team fixed for one waterwheel first installs the waterwheel the night before, and often goes to the waterwheel in the middle of the night, carrying their unrecovered fatigue and empty stomachs, and draws three or four hundred counts of water before dawn to come back for breakfast. The sparse straw curtain is not enough to provide any shade. The skin on their backs, which has been peeled off by the sun, is exposed to the poisonous sun, and their chests, which are covered with prickly heat, lie on the handrails. Their swollen feet stomp on the footrests one by one, and pus drips from the broken blisters on their feet, mixing with the sweat all over their bodies. The so-called "calluses on their hands and feet" cannot even begin to describe their hardship! Therefore, it is common on the waterwheel banks this year for people to suddenly fall from the handrails and die, or to lie down in the willow shade during rest and be unable to get up. Even the healthy ones who don't get sick on the spot can't lift their own legs when they go home at night to receive their wages and go to bed, and need their wives or sons to lift them. But if someone hires them to draw water tomorrow, they are still considered lucky. Alas, the cheap sale of labor and life in this year! Because there are so few opportunities to draw water due to the drought, there are more people than waterwheels. Therefore, the workers who work so hard to draw water all day only earn ten cents of silver.

Finally, I must say that drawing water is quite an artistic endeavor. They often use a primitive form of singing called "counting draws" to hope to forget a little of their fatigue. They nail a pair of white goose feathers to a Lianbi in the trough as a mark, called the "dragon head." When they start stepping on the waterwheel to turn the axle, everyone sings a sentence together in a tune that is only sound and whose meaning is no longer distinguishable. Then, the first person on the left or right sings a number according to the rotation of the dragon head, called "counting draws." When it reaches ten turns, the person counting the draws sings a tune asking the person on that end to "count the draws." Then, the person counting the draws sings a reply, and the whole team sings in unison. The person counting the draws sings another sentence, and the whole team sings in unison again. This is called "returning the draws." In this way, they continue to count down in order from the second person, and return and sing again after ten turns. Although the tune is monotonous and the sentences have no other meaningful content other than counting, the singing together and the alternating responses can indeed forget some of the pain of work. This is the origin and function of art! Because they have a number in mind as they step, they can sing the numbers without having to pay attention to the up and down movement of the dragon head. There are also those who beat drums and sing simple "flower drum opera tunes," which are mostly Hakka people from Hunan. There are also those who do not count or sing, but use a line wound on the waterwheel to count the draws.

According to official labor, one can stop after drawing one thousand and five counts of water every day. But in this severe drought this year, the bosses demand that they draw one thousand five hundred or six hundred counts, or even keep drawing all day without counting.

Timely Article

Odds and Ends from the Summer Training Course by Lu Menghen 219

The Shanghai Education Bureau's Second Summer Training Course was held from July 9th to July 21st, totaling two weeks. Despite the hot weather, about 200 elementary school teachers from private schools registered to participate. During these two weeks, I saw and heard many interesting things. Now I will write down some odds and ends from the meeting, which may be enough to relieve the readers' boredom in their spare time.

Most of the trainees in the training course are between the ages of 20 and 40. The most distinctive is an old man over 60 years old, with white hair and beard, who still comes to listen to the lectures. When the lecturer says a sentence, he nods his head, seeming to listen with great interest. There is also a girl, about 16 years old, still childish, jumping and eating her chewing gum, which is a fun contrast with the old man's white hair and red face.

The venue is located in Wuben Girls' Middle School on Huangjiaque Road in Ximen, but most of the trainees live in Hongkou. The journey is so far that they can only take the tram instead of walking. Taking the tram is essential to having coppers. When packing coppers in newspaper, the paper often breaks. So during the lecture, you can often hear the sound of copper falling to the ground. A joker said, "This is a big spend of money."

Special lectures are held every day from 1:30 PM to 5:30 PM, and the association invites celebrities from Shanghai to give lectures. That day was probably the 12th. The association invited Mr. Li Tingan, the director of the Health Bureau, to give a lecture on "Education and Hygiene." Director Li arrived at the meeting at 1:45. Before the lecture, Director Li first explained the reason for his late arrival. He said: "Now we are implementing the New Life Movement, and appointments must be kept on time. I have always been the most punctual. Today, because my watch was broken, I didn't know the time. I rushed to buy a new watch and came, but I didn't know that I was 15 minutes late." After he said that, he took out his new watch for everyone to see. All the trainees laughed.

The lecturers hired by the association are all university professors and writers. They either wear robes or suits. Only Mr. Shao Shuangqiu, the dean of the Education College of Daxia University, who teaches the subject of "Elementary School Organization and Administration," is not constrained by small matters and comes to the lecture hall wearing short clothes and pants. There is already a fan behind the platform on the platform, but the old gentleman is fanning in front with a big fan. Perhaps because the old gentleman is fat and afraid of heat, he needs to cool off both in front and behind.

Recently, the weather has been hot. In addition, all the trainees come early to listen to the lectures. In the afternoon, most of them look tired and sleepy. If there is no vigilance and interest, it is necessary to remind people's spirits. No matter how interesting the lecturer says, the listeners are scarce, and they are doing their sleepiness. "Elementary School Multi-Grade Teaching Method" is taught by Mr. Wei Bingxin, the editor of the World Book Company. Mr. Wei, in order to remind everyone's spirit, said a joke: "The multi-grade teaching method is not very popular now, just like old antiques. To cater to the trend, we should teach modern things. Old antiques must be modernized, like an old woman with chicken skin and white hair, wearing fashionable clothes and high-heeled leather shoes." All the trainees laughed after hearing these jokes, like they had been injected with morphine, and they really perked up.

There are many other interesting things, but because of the limited space, I have to omit them.

By the Stove · Fei · Fei 222

Scientific Industry Talks About the Story of the Invention of Airships (8) Shulin 223

When Huboto was dying, Zeppelin sat beside his bed, holding his hand tightly.

The younger brother also held the elder brother's hand tightly, looking at his face, but his eyes were already scattered. He said in a trembling voice:

"Brother...airship...Brother...airship..."

These were Huboto's last words, spoken intermittently, and then he passed away.

Zeppelin, with his white hair fluttering, was devastated, and the whole family could not help but weep quietly.

If Huboto had been given time, helping his brother day and night to engage in the production of airships, perhaps he would have been able to fly and swim leisurely on Lake Constance! At that time, how overjoyed and immersed in the encouragement of life would Huboto have been! But in the middle of his career, he passed away!

However, Huboto's death was not without meaning.

The world began to pay attention to Zeppelin's career. They invested their efforts. The world also gradually had considerable respect for Zeppelin's career, for which his younger brother sacrificed.

"For the airship..." "For the new German airship..." "To commemorate Huboto's airship..."

Under this name, the world worked hard to invest, and Zeppelin suddenly gathered huge sums of money in his hands.

In addition, Emperor Wilhelm of Germany at that time also focused on Zeppelin's airship, believing that it would serve the empire in the future, and assisted with huge funds as a public advocate, and even built a hangar and engine.

Zeppelin's courage greatly increased, and he resumed the manufacture of the airship. After several failures, he completed the completely Zeppelin-style airship. (To be continued)
